اشرف النعوت شرح مسلم الثبوت
1.2
جواب :۔ یہ ہے کہ ہر فن میں مقاصد کے علاوہ بہت سی ایسی چیزیں تبعا بطور تمہ اور فن کی غایات مقصودہ کی اصلاح و درستگی کے لئے ذکر کی جاتی ہیں لہذا بعض احوال کا احکام کی طرف راجع ہونا مستلزم نہیں اس بات کو کہ احکام اصول فقہ کا موضوع ہیں یہی مذہب جمہور کا ہے اور مصنف کا مذہب مختار اور امام ابن الحمام کا بھی یہی پسندیدہ ہے اور احکام میں آمدی نے بھی اس پر جزم کیا ہے مگر ان سے احکام کی بھی روایت منقول ہے۔
Ashraf al-Nu'ut Sharh Musallam al-Thubut. The author refutes all those who consider ahkam to be the subject. He says: The truth is that ahkam are not the subject. As for the mention of ahkam in this art, the purpose of that mention is to depict and classify ahkam, i.e., to explain the meaning of hukm and the states particular to it, so that a distinction is achieved and the types of evidences (adillah) can be established from the types of ahkam, so that further discussion and clarification can occur. For example, the usuli mentions the types of hukm: wujub, hurmah, jawaz, karahah, nadb, so that it becomes known that wujub is established by a qat'i proof, and karahah by a zanni proof, or that by this proof the category of 'azimah is established, and by that proof the category of rukhsah is derived, etc. In summary, the usuliyun discuss only the aspect of how the evidence indicates the signified (madlul), and it is clear that 'indication' (dalalah) is a state of the evidence. Therefore, the states that are often mentioned in usul al-fiqh regarding indication refer back to the evidences, so the evidences are the primary intention, whose states are discussed in this art. Then there is an objection: Sadr al-Shari'ah said that consideration is the ruling factor: some states discussed in this art refer back to evidences, while others refer back to rulings; so considering some as intended and others as introductory or subsidiary is arbitrary. The answer: In every art, besides the intended ends, many things are mentioned as subsidiary, by way of introduction, and for the correction and refinement of the intended ends. Therefore, some states referring back to rulings does not entail that rulings are the subject of usul al-fiqh. This is the position of the majority, and it is the chosen position of the author and also of Imam Ibn al-Humam, and al-Amidi also asserted it, though a narration from him says the opposite.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (ikhtilaf) about the subject matter (mawdu') of usul al-fiqh. The author first notes that some, like al-Ghazali, confined the subject to ahkam but that was due to the fame of adillah as the subject. Then the author states the correct view: ahkam are not the subject; they are mentioned only for typification and classification, so that the types of evidences can be derived from the types of rulings. For example, wujub is proven by qat'i evidence, karahah by zanni evidence. The usuli discusses the states of dalalah (indication), which are states of the evidence, so adillah are the primary object. A hypothetical objection is raised: since some states refer to rulings, they should also be part of the subject. The answer is that every science includes things as subsidiary introductions, so that does not make them the subject. The author adopts the majority view, shared by Ibn al-Humam.

Key Terms
موضوع (mawdu'): The primary object or subject matter of a discipline, that which is studied essentially and directly.
دلالت (dalalah): Indication, the property of a proof that signals a ruling; a state of the evidence.
احکام (ahkam): Rulings of Shari'ah; in this context, the categories like wujub, hurmah, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, why are ahkam (e.g., wujub, haram) mentioned in usul al-fiqh?
A) Because they are the primary subject of the science.
B) To classify rulings so that types of evidences can be derived from them.
C) To provide a complete list of all fiqh rulings.
D) Because they are needed for the definition of usul al-fiqh.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school definitively holds that the subject of usul al-fiqh is the evidences (adillah), not the rulings (ahkam); ahkam are introduced only for classification.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
10 min
Can Theoretical Reasoning Produce Certain Knowledge? The Hanafi Position
Debate on whether sound nazar produces certain knowledge of reality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the epistemic value of nazar, explain the skeptic objection, and identify the Mu'tazila response and its critique.

Core Idea
Sound reasoning (nazar sahih) yields certain knowledge; skepticism about nazar is self-defeating.

The reliability of theoretical reasoning (nazar) is a foundational issue in usul al-fiqh, because it underpins the use of rational proofs like qiyas. Skeptics argue that nazar often leads to error, so it cannot produce certain knowledge. The Hanafi school, along with the majority of rationalists, affirms that sound nazar, when conditions are met, does yield certain knowledge. In this lesson, we explore the argument, the self-refutation of skepticism, and a subtle critique of the Mu'tazila's attempt to distinguish knowledge from ignorance by accidents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the skeptic position
State the claim of the Samaniyya/Mulahida: nazar cannot produce certain knowledge because contradictory results show its unreliability. Note their challenge: how do you know your nazar is sound when ignorance obtained through nazar looks identical to knowledge?
2
Analyze the Hanafi-majority response
The jumhur holds that nazar sahih (meeting all conditions) necessarily produces knowledge. Taftazani points out that the skeptics' own argument relies on reasoning, making it self-defeating. Also, sense-perception also errs, so their alternative fails.
This is a key argument: if all reasoning is flawed, then the argument against reasoning is also flawed.
3
Examine the Mu'tazila response
The Mu'tazila concede that knowledge and ignorance from nazar are identical in essence but argue they can be distinguished by their accidents (awarid). The rational faculty (badahah) then judges which is which.
The author presents this response critically, introducing it with 'yujab' to show disapproval.
4
Understand the author's objection
The author argues that the Mu'tazila assume we can identify which reasoning is sound, but this is precisely what is in question. The possibility of error in premises means we have no independent way to verify soundness, leading to a regress.
The objection targets the Mu'tazila's reliance on badahah as a criterion: how do we know the badahah itself is not mistaken?
5
Derive the lesson for usul al-fiqh
The dispute directly affects the validity of rational proofs (adilla aqliyya) in fiqh. If nazar is unreliable, qiyas and istihsan are undermined. The Hanafi school affirms their validity when conditions are met, but emphasizes the need for rigorous methodology.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that Hanafi usul accepts qiyas as a valid source of law, while extreme skeptics would reject it.

ہوسکتا اگر کسی سے علم حاصل ہو سکتا ہے تو وہ صرف حس ہے ان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ نظر سے جو جزم حاصل ہوتا ہے وہ کبھی خلاف واقعہ بھی ہوتا ہے اور یہ سراسر جہل ہے اور یہ جہل جو بعد نظر حاصل ہوا ہے بعینہ اس علم واقع مطابق کی طرح ہے جو علم کہ نظر کے بعد حاصل ہوتا ہے پس جب نظر سے علم و جہل دونوں حاصل ہوتے ہیں تو پھر کس طرح یہ معلوم ہو سکے گا کہ نظر سے جو ہم کو حاصل ہوا ہے علم ہی ہے جہل نہیں جسمغنیہ کی دلیل کی مزید توضیح یہ ہے کہ نظر کے بعد جو جزم حاصل ہوتا ہے اس میں اکثر غلطیاں ہو جایا کرتی ہیں کہ نظر سے حاصل شدہ علم کے بارے میں آراء متناقض ہیں چنانچہ بہت سے عقلاء نظر کرتے ہیں تو اس کو اس نظر سے ایسا مطلوب حاصل ہوتا ہے جو ناظر اول کے مطلوب سے مناقض ہوتا ہے اور یہ بدیہی ہے کہ بیک وقت دونوں مطلوب ایک واقعہ کے مطابق نہیں ہو سکتے ورنہ اجتماع نقیضین لازم آئے گا اور یہ محال اور جوستلزم محال ہے وہ محال ہوتا ہے لہذا نظر سے واقع کے مطابق علم کا حاصل ہونا محال ہے یہی مذہب ملاحدہ کا ہے اور باب الہیاب میں فلاسفہ کا بھی یہی نظریہ ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف جمہور عقلاء کا مذہب مختار یہ ہے کہ ہر وہ نظر جو صیح ہو تجمع شرائط ہو اور مواقع سب مرتفع ہوں وہ تصورات، خواہ تصدیقات البیہ وغیرہ سب میں علم کا افادہ کرتا ہے کیونکہ جو شخص نظر صحیح مستجمع شرائط پر نظر رکھے اور ساتھ ہی حال لازم اس کے پیش نظر رہے تو اس کو جزم حاصل ہوتا ہے کہ بر نظر صیح علم بالجزم کا دابتہ افادہ کرتا ہے۔ رہے نا فین کا یہ کہنا کہ حصول علم کا ذریعہ صرف حس سے صحیح نہیں اولا اس لئے کہ ہمکو بدیہات کا علم حاصل ہوتا ہے جن میں حس کو مطلقا دخل نہیں جیسے ہمارا قول کل مضايفة لا يوجد بدون الآخر ثانیا حس بھی بے شمار غلطیاں کرتا ہے چنانچہ حائے بصر، صغیر کو کبیر ، کبیر کوصغیر واحد کو اثنین اور اثنین کو اربعہ دیکھتا ہے، یونہی حاسہ ذائقہ میٹھا کو کڑوا پاتا ہے وغیرہ ۔ غرض بذریعہ حس علم حاصل ہونے کے بعد جو جزم حاصل ہوتا ہے وہ کبھی جہل ، غیر مطابق للواقع ہوتا ہے اس لئے حس بھی اس جزم کا افادہ نہیں کر سکتا جو جس کہ علم مطابق للواقع کا جزم پیدا کرتا ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ نظر کی طرح جس کے ذریعہ حاصل شدہ جہل بھی علم کے مثل ہو گیا تو پھر کیسے جانا جائے گا کہ۔ جس کے ذریعہ جو حاصل ہوا ہے وہ علم ہی ہے جہل نہیں ۔ فما هو جوابكم فهو جوابنا - شرح عقائد میں علامہ سعدالدین تفتازانی نے سمعیہ و ملاحدہ کے نظریہ کا بطلان کرتے ہوئے کہا ہے کہ بعض نظر کا فساد کے سبب مفید علم نہ ہونا اسبات کی دلیل نہیں بن سکتی کہ ہر نظر صحیح تجمع شرائط بھی مفید علم نہیں ہے علاوہ ازیں جو تم نے نفی نظر پر استدلال کیا ہے وہ نظر عقل ہی سے ہے تو اسمیں اسی بات کا اثبات ہے جسکی نفی کر چکے ہو یعنی دعوی تھا نظر عقلی کے علم کے افادہ کی نفی کا اور نفی پر جو دلیل تم نے ذکر کی ہے وہ نظر عقل ہی سے ثابت ہے غرض تمہارا قول اول ( دعوی ) تمہارے قول آخر دلیل کے مناقض ہے۔

قوله ويجاب بانه يتميز بالعوارض فان البداهة تحكم الخ. اس عبارت سے سمنیہ وغیرہ عسکرین نظر کے اعتراض کا جواب معتزلہ کی طرف سے دیا گیا ہے۔ معتزلہ کا یہ جواب مصنف کے نزدیک نا پسندیدہ ہے اس لئے یجاب سے ذکر کیا۔ معتزلہ کا جواب : معتزلہ کہتے ہیں کہ ہم کو تسلیم ہے کہ نظر سے حاصل شدہ علم و جہل حقیقت و ماہیت کے اعتبار سے متفق و متحد ہیں تاہم ان دنوں متماثلاث کے درمیان امتیاز مشکل نہیں کیونکہ علم و جہل کے عوارض و لوازم مختلف ہوتے ہیں پس یہ متماثلات اپنے اپنے عوارض ولوازم کے مختلف و ممتاز ہونے کے اعتبار سے ایک دوسرے سے ممتاز ہو جائیں گے، چنانچہ نظر صحیح کے بعد ان عوارض کے ملاحظہ کر لینے کے بعد ، بدایت عقلیہ حکم لگا دیتی ہے کہ وہ علم ہے جہل نہیں ، اور ماھیت نوعیہ کے افراد و اشخاص بھی عوارض ہی کے ذریعہ مختلف ہوتے ہیں اور اسی سے عقل کے نزدیک ماهیت کے اعتبار سے بھی ممتاز گردانے جاتے ہیں لہذا یہ کہنا کہ جہل علم کی طرح ہو جائے گا تو امتیاز نہیں ہو سکے گا صحیح نہیں ۔ قوله "اقول وفيه انه بماذا يعلم انه نظر صحيح فان الاحتمال الخ درج بالا عبارت میں جواب معتزلہ پر مصنف کا اعتراض مذکور ہے۔
تقریر اعتراض :- یہ ہے کہ معتزلہ کایہ کہنا کہ نظر صحیح کے وقت بدایت عقلیہ حکم لگا دیتی ہے کہ یہ لم ہے جہل نہیں ، غلط ہے کیونکہ اولاً نظر ہی میں کلام ہے کہ جس نظر کو حصول علم یا حصول مطلوب کے لئے ترتیب دیا ہے کیا پتہ کہ وہ نظر بھی صحیح ہے کہ نہیں ، اس لئے کہ خطاء اور جہل کا احتمال جس طرح مطالب و مقاصد میں رہتا ہے بعینہ اسی طرح دلائل و مقدمات میں بھی خطاء کا احتمال برابر رہتا ہے تو پھر کیسے جانا جا سکے گا کہ وہ نظر صحیح ہے اور دوسرا فاسد ہے اور جب نظر صحیح ونظر فاسد کے درمیان فرق ہی نہیں ہو سکتا تو اس نظر سے کیسے علم ہو گا ۔
It is possible that knowledge can only be obtained through sense-perception. Their argument is that the certainty (jasm) obtained from reasoning (nazar) sometimes contradicts reality, and that is sheer ignorance, and this ignorance obtained after reasoning is exactly like the knowledge that conforms to reality obtained after reasoning. So when both knowledge and ignorance are obtained from reasoning, how can it be known that what we obtained from reasoning is knowledge and not ignorance? A further elaboration of the Samaniyya argument is that the certainty obtained after reasoning often contains errors, and opinions about knowledge obtained from reasoning are contradictory. Many rational people reason and obtain from that reasoning a desired conclusion that contradicts the desired conclusion of the first reasoner. It is self-evident that both desired conclusions cannot simultaneously correspond to one reality, otherwise there would be a conjunction of opposites, which is impossible. Whatever leads to the impossible is itself impossible. Therefore, obtaining knowledge corresponding to reality from reasoning is impossible. This is the doctrine of the Mulahida and also the view of the philosophers in Ilahiyyat. Contrary to this, the chosen doctrine of the majority of rationalists is that every sound reasoning that meets all conditions and removes all obstacles produces knowledge in conceptualizations (tasawwurat) and even self-evident affirmations (tasdiqat). Because the person who engages in sound reasoning with all conditions and keeps in mind the necessary state will obtain certainty that sound reasoning necessarily produces certain knowledge. As for the opponents' claim that the means of obtaining knowledge is only sense-perception, it is incorrect. First, because we obtain knowledge of self-evident matters in which sense has no part, like our statement 'every relative cannot exist without the other.' Second, sense also makes countless errors. Thus the sense of sight sees small as large, large as small, one as two, two as four. Similarly, the sense of taste finds sweet as bitter, etc. In short, the certainty obtained after sense-perception sometimes is ignorance, not conforming to reality. Therefore sense also cannot produce that certainty which is knowledge conforming to reality. The result is that just like reasoning, the ignorance obtained through it becomes similar to knowledge, so how can it be known that what is obtained is knowledge and not ignorance? 'So your answer is our answer.' In the Sharh al-Aqa'id, 'Allama Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani, refuting the view of the Samaniyya and Mulahida, said that the fact that some reasoning does not produce knowledge due to corruption cannot be proof that every sound reasoning that meets conditions also does not produce knowledge. Moreover, your argument against reasoning itself is based on rational reasoning, so it proves exactly what you have denied. That is, you claimed to negate the efficacy of rational reasoning in producing knowledge, and the proof you mentioned for that negation is established by rational reasoning. In sum, your first statement (the claim) contradicts your last statement (the proof).

His statement: 'And it is answered that it is distinguished by accidents, for self-evident reason judges...' This phrase presents the response of the Mu'tazila to the objection of the Samaniyya and others concerning reasoning. This response of the Mu'tazila is disapproved by the author, so he mentions it with 'yujab' (it is answered). The response of the Mu'tazila: The Mu'tazila say: We concede that the knowledge and ignorance obtained from reasoning are identical in essence and reality. Nevertheless, distinguishing between these two similar things is not difficult because the accidents (awarid) and concomitants (lawazim) of knowledge and ignorance differ. Therefore these similars become distinguished from each other by virtue of the difference of their accidents and concomitants. Thus, after sound reasoning, after observing these accidents, the rational faculty judges that it is knowledge and not ignorance. The individuals of a specific essence are also differentiated by accidents, and by this they are distinguished in the view of the intellect with respect to essence. Hence the claim that ignorance, being similar to knowledge, cannot be distinguished, is incorrect.

His statement: 'I say: In it, how is it known that it is sound reasoning? For probability...' The above phrase contains the author's objection to the Mu'tazila's response.

Presentation of the objection: The Mu'tazila's claim that at the time of sound reasoning, the rational faculty judges that this is knowledge and not ignorance, is false. Because firstly, there is dispute about the reasoning itself: the reasoning we have arranged to obtain knowledge or the desired result, how do we know that that reasoning is sound? For the possibility of error and ignorance exists in the premises and conclusions just as it exists in the desired results and objectives. So how can it be known that this reasoning is sound and that one is corrupt? And when there is no distinction between sound and corrupt reasoning, how can knowledge be obtained from this reasoning?
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage presents a crucial usul al-fiqh dispute about the epistemic value of theoretical reasoning (nazar). The text begins by stating the argument of the Samaniyya and Mulahida that reasoning cannot produce certain knowledge because it often leads to error. They use the problem of contradictory conclusions from different reasoners to argue that certainty is impossible through reasoning. The majority of rationalists, including the Hanafi school, respond that sound reasoning that meets all conditions does produce certain knowledge. Taftazani refutes the skeptics by pointing out the self-defeating nature of their argument: their own reasoning against reasoning is itself an act of reasoning. Then the Mu'tazila offer a response: knowledge and ignorance, though similar in essence, are distinguished by their different accidents and concomitants, and the rational faculty can judge based on these. The author (Muslih al-Thubut) criticizes the Mu'tazila response, arguing that we cannot know whether a particular reasoning is sound because the possibility of error is always present in premises and arguments themselves. This leads to a skeptical regress. The passage teaches that the Hanafi school affirms the epistemological reliability of sound nazar, while recognizing the need to critically evaluate arguments. The discussion is not merely philosophical but directly impacts how we derive rulings (ahkam) from rational proofs.

Key Terms
نظر (nazar): Theoretical reasoning or contemplation that aims at deriving knowledge from premises
جزم (jasm): Firm certainty or conviction that results from reasoning or sensation
بداہت (badahah): Self-evident or intuitive judgment of the intellect that does not require reasoning
عوارض (awarid): Accidental properties or attributes that are not essential to a thing's nature

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the author's primary objection to the Mu'tazila's response that knowledge and ignorance can be distinguished by their accidents?
A) Accidents are not real properties
B) One cannot know which reasoning is sound to begin with, due to the possibility of error in premises
C) The intellect is incapable of perceiving accidents
D) Accidents are the same for knowledge and ignorance

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school affirms that sound theoretical reasoning (nazar sahih) produces certain knowledge, a position defended against skepticism by the self-refutation argument and critical refinement of the Mu'tazila response.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Does Speculative Reasoning (Nazar) Yield Certain Knowledge? The Hanafi-Mu'tazila Dispute
Refutation of Mu'tazila claim that nazar yields knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on nazar and evaluate the Mu'tazila argument using the Hanafi refutation.

Core Idea
Nazar cannot yield certain knowledge because error always remains possible; knowledge and ignorance are essentially distinct.

This lesson examines a foundational usul dispute: does speculative reasoning (nazar) produce certain knowledge ('ilm)? The Mu'tazila claimed it does, while Hanafi and Ash'ari scholars denied it. The debate goes to the heart of how we can trust our reasoning in deriving rulings. We will trace the arguments and understand why the Hanafi school ultimately rejects the productivity of nazar.

Guided Path
1
State the Mu'tazila claim
Identify what the Mu'tazila assert: that correct nazar, when conditions are fulfilled, yields certain knowledge through the judgment of badaha (primal reason).
The Mu'tazila concede that knowledge and ignorance are similar in essence but distinguish them by accidents.
2
Identify the Hanafi objection
The author objects: how do you know the nazar is correct? The probability of error remains in premises and reasoning; thus you cannot claim certainty.
This leads to an infinite regress if one requires another nazar to verify correctness.
3
Follow the potential sensory certification
The Mu'tazila might argue that sense perception can verify correct nazar. The Hanafi response: sense gives only partial (juz'i) knowledge, not universal certainty.
Partial knowledge is insufficient to certify the entire reasoning process.
4
Analyze the denial of tamathul
The author's final position: knowledge and ignorance are essentially distinct (mutabayin), not similar. Thus badaha cannot mistake one for the other, but the problem of identifying correct nazar remains.
This refutes the Mu'tazila's reliance on distinguishing accidents.
5
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence for ijtihad: if nazar does not yield certainty, then rulings derived solely from rational speculation (without transmitted sources) are not certain. Only Quran, Sunnah, and ijma provide certainty; qiyas and istihsan yield zann.
This is why Hanafis ground their usul in transmitted texts and use reason only within their framework.

سبب مفید علم نہ ہونا اسبات کی دلیل نہیں بن سکتی کہ ہر نظر صحیح تجمع شرائط بھی مفید علم نہیں ہے علاوہ ازیں جو تم نے نفی نظر پر استدلال کیا ہے وہ نظر عقل ہی سے ہے تو اسمیں اسی بات کا اثبات ہے جسکی نفی کر چکے ہو یعنی دعوی تھا نظر عقلی کے علم کے افادہ کی نفی کا اور نفی پر جو دلیل تم نے ذکر کی ہے وہ نظر عقل ہی سے ثابت ہے غرض تمہارا قول اول ( دعوی ) تمہارے قول آخر دلیل کے مناقض ہے۔
قوله ويجاب بانه يتميز بالعوارض فان البداهة تحكم الخ. اس عبارت سے سمنیہ وغیرہ عسکرین نظر کے اعتراض کا جواب معتزلہ کی طرف سے دیا گیا ہے۔ معتزلہ کا یہ جواب مصنف کے نزدیک نا پسندیدہ ہے اس لئے یجاب سے ذکر کیا۔ معتزلہ کا جواب : معتزلہ کہتے ہیں کہ ہم کو تسلیم ہے کہ نظر سے حاصل شدہ علم و جہل حقیقت و ماہیت کے اعتبار سے متفق و متحد ہیں تاہم ان دنوں متماثلاث کے درمیان امتیاز مشکل نہیں کیونکہ علم و جہل کے عوارض و لوازم مختلف ہوتے ہیں پس یہ متماثلات اپنے اپنے عوارض ولوازم کے مختلف و ممتاز ہونے کے اعتبار سے ایک دوسرے سے ممتاز ہو جائیں گے، چنانچہ نظر صحیح کے بعد ان عوارض کے ملاحظہ کر لینے کے بعد ، بدایت عقلیہ حکم لگا دیتی ہے کہ وہ علم ہے جہل نہیں ، اور ماھیت نوعیہ کے افراد و اشخاص بھی عوارض ہی کے ذریعہ مختلف ہوتے ہیں اور اسی سے عقل کے نزدیک ماهیت کے اعتبار سے بھی ممتاز گردانے جاتے ہیں لہذا یہ کہنا کہ جہل علم کی طرح ہو جائے گا تو امتیاز نہیں ہو سکے گا صحیح نہیں ۔ قوله "اقول وفيه انه بماذا يعلم انه نظر صحيح فان الاحتمال الخ درج بالا عبارت میں جواب معتزلہ پر مصنف کا اعتراض مذکور ہے۔
تقریر اعتراض :- یہ ہے کہ معتزلہ کایہ کہنا کہ نظر صحیح کے وقت بدایت عقلیہ حکم لگا دیتی ہے کہ یہ علم ہے جہل نہیں ، غلط ہے کیونکہ اولاً نظر ہی میں کلام ہے کہ جس نظر کو حصول علم یا حصول مطلوب کے لئے ترتیب دیا ہے کیا پتہ کہ وہ نظر بھی صحیح ہے کہ نہیں ، اس لئے کہ خطاء اور جہل کا احتمال جس طرح مطالب و مقاصد میں رہتا ہے بعینہ اسی طرح دلائل و مقدمات میں بھی خطاء کا احتمال برابر رہتا ہے تو پھر کیسے جانا جا سکے گا کہ وہ نظر صحیح ہے اور دوسرا فاسد ہے اور جب نظر صحیح ونظر فاسد کے درمیان فرق ہی نہیں ہو سکتا تو اس نظر سے کیسے علم ہو گا ۔
قوله " والحس لايفيد الاعلماً جزئياً وهولايكون كاسباً مصنف کے ذکر کردہ اعتراض پر ایک اعتراض وارد ہوتا ہے اس عبارت سے مائن نے اس اعتراض کا جواب دیا ہے اعتراض و جواب کی تقریر مندرجہ ذیل ہے۔ اعتراض :- یہ ہے کہ ماتن کا یہ کہنا کہ خطاء غلطی کا احتمال مبادی سے مقاطع تک اور دلائل سے مطالب تک برابر رہتا ہے اس لئے مبادی یا دلائل و نظر کے بارے میں یقینی طور پر یہ نہیں کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ صحیح ہے، درست نہیں کیونکہ ایسا ممکن ہے کہ مبادی علوم حسی ہوں یعنی نظر کی صحت و درستگی حس سے یا ان مقدمات سے معلوم ہو جائے جس کا تعلق جس سے ہے چونکہ معتزلہ و سمعیہ کوئی بھی جس سے انکار نہیں کرتے۔ جواب :۔ ماتن اعتراض مذکور کا جواب اپنے قول والحس لا یفید" سے دیتے ہوئے کہتے ہیں کہ جس سے زیادہ سے زیادہ علم جزئی حاصل ہو سکتا ہے اور علم جزئی نہ کا سب ہوتا ہے نہ مکتب پس حس سے بالکلیہ صحت نظر کی درستگی کا علم نہیں ہو سکتا۔ مصنف نے اس مقام پر حاشیہ میں اسی مضمون کو بایں الفاظ ذکر کیا ہے۔
جواب سوال وهوانه يجوز أن يكون مقاطع العلم علوماً حسية ومقاطع الجهل علوماً عقلية فأجاب بأن العلوم الحسية علوم جزئية لاتكون كاسبة فلا كاسب الاعلوما عقلية
قوله بل الحق منع التماثل كماهو مذهنبا
سمنیہ کا جواب اور معتزلہ پر رد کرتے ہوئے محققین نے جواب دیا ہے جس کو مصنف نے اپنے قول " بل الحق منع التماثل" سے بیان کیا۔ اسکا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے کہ جہل علم کی طرح ہے کہ ایک دوسرے سے ممتاز نہیں ہو سکتا۔ بلکہ حق یہ ہے کہ وہ دونوں حقیقت و ماهیت کے اعتبار سے دونوں متبائن ہیں گوکہ نفس جزم میں دونوں مشترک ہوتے ہیں لیکن وہ دونوں جزم ایک دوسرے سے اپنے لوازم و خواص کے اعتبار سے ممتاز ہو جایا کرتے ہیں چنانچہ ناظر، مقدمات صادقہ صحیحہ کا عالم اور ترتیب نظر مفضی الی المطلوب کا جان کار فی البدیہہ جانتا ہے کہ جو حاصل ہوا ہے اس نظر سے علم ہے جہل نہیں۔
The fact that something is not productive of knowledge cannot serve as a proof of its negation, because every correct nazar that fulfills all conditions is also not productive of knowledge. Moreover, your argument against nazar is itself based on intellectual nazar, so it proves exactly what you deny: you claimed that intellectual nazar does not produce knowledge, and the proof you gave for its negation is established through intellectual nazar. Thus your first statement (the claim) contradicts your last statement (the proof). He said: 'The answer is that it is distinguished by accidents, for badaha judges...' With this phrase, the answer of the Mu'tazila to the objection of the Samaniyya and others concerning nazar is given. This answer of the Mu'tazila is disapproved by the author, therefore he mentioned it with 'yujabu'. The Mu'tazila's answer: The Mu'tazila say: We concede that the knowledge and ignorance obtained from nazar are in agreement and united in essence and quiddity, yet distinguishing between these two similars is not difficult because the accidents and necessary concomitants of knowledge and ignorance differ. So these similars will be distinguished from each other by virtue of their accidents and necessary concomitants being different and distinct. Thus after correct nazar and observing these accidents, badaha (primal reason) judges that it is knowledge, not ignorance. Moreover, the individuals of a specific quiddity also differ through accidents, and by this they are distinguished in the view of reason in terms of quiddity. Therefore, saying that ignorance will be like knowledge and thus distinction is impossible is not correct. He said: 'I say: And therein is that how is it known that it is correct nazar? For probability...' In the above phrase, the author's objection to the Mu'tazila's answer is mentioned. The presentation of the objection: This is that the Mu'tazila's statement that at the time of correct nazar, badaha judges it to be knowledge not ignorance is false, because firstly there is discussion about the nazar itself: what was intended to obtain knowledge or the desired thing? How is it known whether that nazar is correct or not? For the probability of error and ignorance remains in premises and proofs just as it remains in objectives and aims. So how can it be known that this nazar is correct and the other is corrupt? And when there is no distinction between correct and corrupt nazar, how can knowledge be obtained from it? He said: 'And sense does not produce anything except partial knowledge, and it is not profitable.' An objection is raised against this objection mentioned by the author. With this phrase, the author answers that objection. The presentation of the objection and answer is as follows: Objection: This is that the author's statement that the probability of error remains from the beginnings to the ends and from the proofs to the objectives is not correct, because it is possible that the beginnings are sensory sciences, i.e., the correctness of nazar can be known through sense or through those premises related to it, and neither the Mu'tazila nor the Samaniyya deny sense. Answer: The author answers this objection with his statement 'And sense does not produce anything except partial knowledge' and says that sense at most gives partial knowledge, and partial knowledge is neither profitable nor stated. Thus through sense, knowledge of the absolute correctness of nazar cannot be obtained. The author has mentioned the same content in the margin with these words: 'The answer to the question is that it is permissible that the ends of knowledge are sensory sciences and the ends of ignorance are intellectual sciences. So he answered that sensory sciences are partial sciences that are not profitable; so nothing is profitable except intellectual sciences.' He said: 'But the truth is the denial of similarity, as is our doctrine.' The Samaniyya's answer and refutation of the Mu'tazila: The investigators have given an answer, which the author expressed with his statement 'But the truth is the denial of similarity.' Its summary is that we do not concede that ignorance is like knowledge such that they cannot be distinguished. Rather, the truth is that both are disparate in essence and quiddity, although both share in the fact of being a judgment, they are distinguished by their necessary concomitants and properties. Thus the nazir, who knows the true correct premises and the arrangement of nazar leading to the desired, knows intuitively that what is obtained from this nazar is knowledge, not ignorance.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is part of a dispute on whether speculative reasoning (nazar) can yield certain knowledge. The author sides with the Ash'ari position that nazar is not productive of knowledge, against the Mu'tazila who claim it does. The passage follows a dialectical structure: First, an objection by the Samaniyya (skeptics) that if nazar cannot produce knowledge, then the proof against it itself uses nazar, leading to contradiction. The author presents the Mu'tazila's response: that knowledge and ignorance, though similar in essence, are distinguished by their accidental properties (awarid), and primal reason (badaha) judges after correct nazar. Then the author objects: how do we know which nazar is correct? Since error remains possible in premises as well, we cannot be certain. A further objection is raised: perhaps the correctness is known through sense perception. The author replies that sense gives only partial (juz'i) knowledge, not the universal certainty required for complete trust in nazar. Finally, the author gives his own position: the truth is to deny similarity (tamathul) between knowledge and ignorance—they are fundamentally different in essence, though they share the form of a judgment. The nazir who has mastered correct premises and proper arrangement immediately knows the result is knowledge.

Key Terms
نظر (nazar): Speculative reasoning aimed at acquiring knowledge or a desired conclusion.
تماثل (tamathul): Likeness in essence; the claim that knowledge and ignorance are essentially the same.
بداهة (badaha): Primal reason or immediate intuition that judges without deliberation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's final position, what is the relationship between knowledge and ignorance?
A) They are identical in essence but differ in accidents.
B) They are essentially distinct (mutabayin).
C) They are similar but can be distinguished by primal reason.
D) They are both products of correct nazar.

Key Takeaway
Speculative reasoning (nazar) cannot produce certain knowledge because error always remains possible and knowledge and ignorance are essentially distinct.

Refining the Denial of Likeness: Tamathul vs. Tashabuh
Critique of author's denial of tamathul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between tamathul (real identity) and tashabuh (similarity in properties) and evaluate when the Hanafi denial of tamathul is correct.

Core Idea
Denying tamathul between knowledge and ignorance is valid only if the opponent means real identity, not mere property similarity.

This passage refines the Hanafi position on whether knowledge and ignorance are alike. The author simply denies tamathul, but the commentator warns that this only works against those who claim real identity (like the Mu'tazila). If the opponent means mere similarity in properties (tashabuh), the denial is insufficient. Understanding this nuance prevents overstating the Hanafi claim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What is the point of dispute? The Samaniyya and Mu'tazila claim that knowledge and ignorance are alike (tamathul). The author denies this (بل الحق منع التماثل).
2
Distinguish two meanings of likeness
Likeness can mean real identity in essence (tamathul haqiqi) or similarity in properties and accidents (tashabuh). The commentator clarifies this distinction.
The key is that the author's denial targets tamathul haqiqi.
3
Evaluate the author's answer
The commentator argues: if the opponent meant real identity, the denial is correct and is the Ahl al-Sunnah position. If they meant similarity in properties, the denial does not refute them because at the initial stage of reasoning, knowledge and ignorance are not distinguishable.
The phrase 'فَتَدَبَّر' (so reflect) signals the insufficiency.
4
Apply the evaluation
The student should conclude that the Hanafi position is nuanced: we reject real identity but acknowledge similarity in initial judgment (jazm). The correct response depends on the opponent's intended meaning.

قوله بل الحق منع التماثل كماهو مذهنبا سمنیہ کا جواب اور معتزلہ پر رد کرتے ہوئے محققین نے جواب دیا ہے جس کو مصنف نے اپنے قول " بل الحق منع التماثل" سے بیان کیا۔ اسکا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے کہ جہل علم کی طرح ہے کہ ایک دوسرے سے ممتاز نہیں ہو سکتا۔ بلکہ حق یہ ہے کہ وہ دونوں حقیقت و ماهیت کے اعتبار سے دونوں متبائن ہیں گوکہ نفس جزم میں دونوں مشترک ہوتے ہیں لیکن وہ دونوں جزم ایک دوسرے سے اپنے لوازم و خواص کے اعتبار سے ممتاز ہو جایا کرتے ہیں چنانچہ ناظر، مقدمات صادقہ صحیحہ کا عالم اور ترتیب نظر مفضی الی المطلوب کا جان کار فی البدیہہ جانتا ہے کہ جو حاصل ہوا ہے اس نظر سے علم ہے جہل نہیں۔ قوله فتدبر سے اشارہ ہے کہ سمنیہ کے رد میں جواب مذکور بھی نا کافی ہے کیونکہ علم و جہل کے ما بین تماثل کا قول کرنے سے سمنیہ کی مراد تشابہ ہے یعنی خواص و اعراض کے اعتبار سے علم و جہل متحد ہوتا ہے بایں طور کہ ابتدائے امر میں علم و جہل اس حیثیت سے ہوتے ہیں کہ ایک دوسرے سے ممتاز نہیں ہوتے اور اس میں شک نہیں کہ ابتداء علم و جہل نظر سے حاصل ہونے کے بعد جزم حاصل ہونے کے اعتبار سے ایک طرح ہوتے ہیں چنانچہ جو جزم نظر سے حاصل ہوتا ہے کبھی علم ہوتا ہے اور وہی کبھی جہل ہوتا ہے اس طرح اول امر میں دونوں ایک دوسرے سے ممتاز نہیں ہو پاتے ۔ غرض مصنف کا منع التماثل کہنا درست نہیں ۔ ہاں یہ جواب اس وقت درست ہوتا جب سمنیہ کی مراد تماثل سے علم و جہل کے درمیان تماثل حقیقی ہوتی جیسا کہ معتزلہ کا گمان ہے۔ خلاصہ ایراد یہ ہے کہ مستدل نے اگر تماثل سے اتحاد فی الحقیقہ مراد لیا ہے تو اسپر مصنف کا منع وارد کرنا صحیح ہے کیونکہ علم و جہل کے درمیان اتحاد حقیقی ممنوع ہے چنانچہ یہی اہلسنت کا مذہب مختار بھی ہے اور اگر مستدل نے اس سے اتحاد فی الخواص مراد لیا ہے تو یہ جواب فائدہ مند ثابت نہ ہوگا۔
His statement: "But the truth is to deny the likeness, as is our doctrine." The scholars have answered the Samaniyya and refuted the Mu'tazila, which the author expressed with his statement "But the truth is to deny the likeness." Its summary is that we do not accept that ignorance is like knowledge such that they cannot be distinguished. Rather, the truth is that both are distinct in reality and essence, even though in the very act of judgment they share something. However, those judgments become distinguished by their properties and characteristics. Thus the observer, who knows the true premises and the arrangement that leads to the sought matter, knows intuitively that what is obtained from that reasoning is knowledge, not ignorance. His statement "fata'dabbar" indicates that the mentioned answer in refuting the Samaniyya is insufficient because when they speak of likeness, they mean similarity, i.e., knowledge and ignorance are united in terms of properties and accidents, such that in the beginning they are not distinguishable. There is no doubt that initially, after they are obtained through reasoning in terms of the judgment, they are alike. So the judgment from reasoning is sometimes knowledge and sometimes ignorance, so at first they are not distinguishable. Therefore, the author's denial of likeness is not correct. However, this answer would be correct if the Samaniyya meant real likeness, as the Mu'tazila imagine. Summary of the objection: If the disputant meant unity in reality, then the author's denial is correct because real unity is prohibited, and that is the chosen madhhab of Ahl al-Sunnah. But if they meant unity in properties, then this answer is not effective.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage critically examines the author's position on tamathul between knowledge and ignorance. The author denied tamathul, but the commentator argues it is insufficient if the opponent means only similarity in properties (tashabuh) rather than real identity. The author's answer works only if real unity is intended, as the Mu'tazila claim. In that case, the denial is valid because knowledge and ignorance are essentially distinct. If mere similarity in properties is meant, the answer does not refute them because at the initial stage of reasoning the judgment can be either knowledge or ignorance and is not distinguishable. The commentator refines the position by explaining this nuance.

Key Terms
تماثل (tamathul): Likeness or equivalence, implying indistinguishability in essence
تشابہ (tashabuh): Similarity in properties and accidents, not in essence
جزم (jazm): The act of making a judgment after reasoning

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, when is the author's denial of tamathul insufficient?
A) When the opponent means real unity (ittihad fi al-haqiqa)
B) When the opponent means unity in properties (ittihad fi al-khawass)
C) It is always sufficient
D) It is never sufficient

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi denial of tamathul between knowledge and ignorance is valid against claims of real identity, but not against claims of mere similarity in properties.

The Theories of Ifadah: Ash'ari, Mu'tazila, Philosophers, and Razi's Synthesis
Presenting the matn's enumeration of theories on how reasoning produces knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four theories on how reasoning (nazar) produces knowledge (ifadah) and explain Imam al-Razi's chosen position in the context of Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Reasoning produces knowledge necessarily after it, but not from human power nor by divine obligation.

This passage from Muslim al-Thubut presents a foundational usul debate: How does reasoning yield knowledge? The Ash'ari, Mu'tazila, and Philosophers each propose mechanisms—custom, generation, and preparation. Imam al-Razi then synthesizes a view that avoids theological pitfalls while preserving the necessity of knowledge after reflection. Understanding these positions is key to grasping Hanafi epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three main theories and their proponents
Read the passage and list each view: Ash'ari (adah), Mu'tazila (tawlid), Philosophers (i'dad). Note the key terms for each.
The passage also includes Imam al-Razi's view as a fourth, preferred position.
2
Understand the mechanism each proposes
For each view, explain how the knowledge is produced: by divine custom (adah), by generation (tawlid), or by preparation (i'dad). Compare their implications for causality.
Tawlid implies human act directly causes knowledge, which conflicts with Ash'ari occasionalism.
3
Locate Imam al-Razi's critique and his alternative
Razi rejects all three: against Ash'ari (no necessity), against Mu'tazila (human causal power), against Philosophers (emanation). He proposes that knowledge is necessary after reasoning (wajib 'aqibahu) but not from the servant's power nor obligatory upon Allah.
The phrase 'wa hadha ashbah' indicates this view is considered more likely correct.
4
Analyze why Razi's view is considered 'ashbah'
Consider the Hanafi commitment to divine omnipotence and the reliability of reason. Razi's view preserves both: knowledge is a necessary concomitant, but not caused by the servant, nor is Allah compelled.
This aligns with the Hanafi principle that acts of worship are not caused by the servant but are created by Allah.
5
Connect to broader implications for causality and human agency
Reflect on how this debate affects the validity of ijtihad and istidlal. If reasoning necessarily yields knowledge, then a mujtahid can be confident in his conclusion, but without attributing creative power to himself.
This also touches on the Ash'ari concept of kasb (acquisition).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متن المسلم : - مسألة: قال الاشعرى ان الافادة بالعادة اذلا مؤثر الا الله تعالى، بلاوجوب منه ولا عليه والمعتزلة انه بالتوليد كحركة المفتاح بحركة اليد والحكماء انه بطريق الاعداد فانه يعد الذهن اعداداً تاماً ويفيض عليه النتيجة من عام الفيض وجوباً واختار الامام الرازى انه واجب عقيبه وان لم يكن واجباً منه تعالى ابتداء غير متولد منه لانه ليس لقدرة العبد تاثير وهذا اشبه فان لزوم بعض الاشياء للبعض ممالاينكر الاترى ان وجود العرض بدون الجوهر والكلية بدون الاعظمية غير معقول ترجمه : حضرت امام اشعری رضی اللہ عنہ نے فرمایا کہ نظر مطلوب کے علم کا افادہ کرتا ہے عادت الہیہ جاری ہونے کی وجہ سے ، اس لئے کہ اللہ عز شانہ کے علاوہ کوئی مؤثر نہیں ہے افادہ اس کی طرف سے وجو با ہے نہ ہی اس پر واجب ہے۔ اور معتزلہ نے کہا کہ نظر مطلوب کا افادہ بطریق تولید کرتا ہے جیسے حرکت ید سے حرکت مفتاح ، اور حکماء نے کہا کہ نظر بطریق اعداد مطلوب کا افادہ کرتا ہے چونکہ نظر
Text of Muslim al-Thubut: Issue: al-Ash'ari said that ifadah occurs by way of custom, because there is no effect except Allah, without obligation from Him nor upon Him. The Mu'tazila said it is by way of generation, like the movement of a key by the movement of a hand. The philosophers said it is by way of preparation, for it prepares the mind completely and the result flows from the universal emanation necessarily. Imam al-Razi chose that it is necessary after it, even if it is not necessary from Allah in the beginning, nor generated from it, because the power of the servant has no effect. And this is more similar, for the necessary connection of some things to others is not denied. Do you not see that the existence of an accident without a substance and of a whole without the greatest part is inconceivable. Translation: Imam Ash'ari said that reasoning provides knowledge of the sought matter due to the continuation of divine custom, because there is no effect except Allah; ifadah from Him is not obligatory nor is He obligated. The Mu'tazila said that reasoning provides knowledge by way of generation, like the movement of a key by the movement of a hand. The philosophers said that reasoning provides knowledge by way of preparation, because reasoning...
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a direct quotation from the matn presenting three views on how reasoning produces knowledge: Ash'ari (divine custom), Mu'tazila (generation), philosophers (preparation). Imam al-Razi chose a middle view: knowledge is necessary after reasoning, but not from the servant's power nor generated, but a necessary concomitance. This is a key usul dispute about causality and human agency.

Key Terms
افادة (ifadah): The production or conveyance of knowledge from reasoning
عادة (adah): Divine custom; Allah habitually creates knowledge after reasoning
توليد (tawlid): Generation; reasoning naturally generates knowledge as a caused effect
اعداد (i'dad): Preparation; reasoning prepares the mind for knowledge from an external source

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Razi, how does reasoning provide knowledge?
A) By divine custom without necessary connection
B) By generation as a necessary product of reasoning
C) By preparation and necessary flow from a source
D) It is necessary after reasoning but not generated nor obligatory upon Allah

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Razi's view—knowledge is necessary after reasoning but not caused by it nor obligatory upon Allah—is the most compatible with Hanafi usul.

Ash'ari Refutation of Mu'tazili Tawlid in Knowledge Acquisition
Dispute on whether nazar generates knowledge directly (tawlid)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Ash'ari qiyas used to refute the Mu'tazili theory of tawlid and identify the key difference that undermines the initial analogy.

Core Idea
Only Allah creates knowledge; nazar is a means, not a cause.

In this usul dispute, we examine the debate between the Ash'aris (followed by Hanafis) and the Mu'tazila over whether human speculation (nazar) generates knowledge through a causal process called tawlid. The Ash'aris use a qiyas (analogy) between initial nazar and recollection of nazar (tadhakkur) to argue that if tawlid were true, then tadhakkur should also generate knowledge—which even the Mu'tazila deny. However, the validity of this qiyas is challenged by pointing out a crucial difference: tadhakkur occurs after knowledge already exists, making any generated knowledge a repetition. The Ash'aris refine their argument by focusing on a specific type of tadhakkur after heedlessness. This passage trains us in the usul skill of evaluating analogical arguments in theological disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Mu'tazili theory of tawlid
State what tawlid means: one act of an agent gives existence to another act, like the hand's movement generating the key's movement. The Mu'tazila apply this to nazar generating knowledge.
Tawlid is distinct from mubasharah (direct act).
2
Analyze the Ash'ari qiyas
The Ash'aris analogize initial nazar (ibtida' al-nazar) to recollection of nazar (tadhakkur). Since both are acts of nazar, and tadhakkur does not generate knowledge (by consensus), initial nazar should also not generate knowledge.
The 'illa is the shared property of being nazar that entails the required from validity of matter and form.
3
Evaluate the critique of the qiyas
Critics (from Sharh al-Mawaqif) argue that the analogy fails because tadhakkur occurs after knowledge already exists, making generated knowledge a repetition (tahsil al-hasil), while initial nazar occurs before knowledge. This is qiyas ma'a al-fariq.
The difference in temporal order breaks the common 'illa.
4
Understand the Ash'ari refinement from al-Nihaya
The Ash'aris respond by specifying that their argument concerns tadhakkur after heedlessness (ghaflah), where no knowledge currently exists. In that case, tadhakkur also does not generate knowledge, even though no repetition issue arises. Thus the qiyas stands for that specific case.
This shows the importance of precise ma'nā al-illah in qiyas.

اشاعرہ کا یہ قیاس رد کر دیا گیا ہے چنانچہ شرح مواقف کے مقدمہ میں ہے کہ تذکر نظر کا قیاس ابتداء نظر پر صحیح نہیں کیونکہ تذکر سے علم کا حصول کالعدم ہے چونکہ تذکر نظر علم حاصل ہونے کے بعد ہوتا ہے پھر اگر تذکر نظر سے پھر وہی علم حاصل ہو تو تحصیل حاصل لازم آئے گا اس کے برعکس ابتداء نظر علم کے حصول سے پہلے ہوتا ہے پس اگر ابتدائے نظر سے علم حاصل ہو تو تحصیل حاصل لازم نہیں آتا ہے لہذا ابتداء نظر کا قیاس تذکر نظر پر قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔ دفع : اشاعرہ کے ذکر کردہ قیاس پر بجانب معتزلہ جو اعتراض کیا گیا اس اعتراض کا جواب اشاعرہ کی طرف سے نہایہ میں دیا گیا ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اشاعرہ کا کلام، مطلق تذکر نظر کے بارے میں نہیں ہے بلکہ اس تذکر میں ہے جو حصول علم سے غفلت طاری ہو جانے کے بعد حاصل ہوتا ہے اور یہ بہت ظاہر ہے کہ اس تذکر سے پیشتر علم نہیں ہوتا چنانچہ معتزلہ کے نزدیک بھی یہ تذکر مولد علم نہیں، علاوہ
He creates without causes, as happens in extraordinary matters. Exactly the same is the case of knowledge after nazar: the knowledge obtained from nazar is created by Allah, possible, contingent, in need of the true effect. Nazar has no role in the acquisition of knowledge from it, just as water-drinking has no role in quenching and fire has no role in burning, because only that pure essence is the true effect. The conclusion is that the acquisition of knowledge after correct nazar is among the acts of Allah that proceed from Him without obligation and without necessity, voluntarily and by choice. Thus, the acquisition of knowledge from nazar also occurs in this manner, not necessarily or coercively as the philosophers claim, nor is imparting knowledge obligatory upon Allah as the Mu'tazila imagined. His saying: 'And the Mu'tazila [hold] that it is by tawlid, like the movement of the key by the movement of the hand, etc.' Second doctrine: In the above statement, the doctrine of the Mu'tazila is explained. The gist of this doctrine is that knowledge from nazar is obtained by way of tawlid. According to them, the meaning of tawlid is that one act of the agent gives existence to another act, like the existence of the key's movement from the hand's movement. The hand's movement is the essential act of the moving agent from which the other act, the key's movement, necessarily proceeds. Similarly, the agent's essential act is nazar, then nazar gives existence to another act, the acquisition of the result. So both nazar and the result are two acts of the same agent, but the hand's movement and nazar proceed directly from the mover and the observer, while the result and the key's movement proceed indirectly through nazar and hand's movement by tawlid. Note: The basis of this flawed idea of the Mu'tazila is established on another corrupt theory of theirs, namely, that the servant is the creator of his own acts, whether those acts proceed from the servant directly or indirectly. If the acts proceed from the servants directly, they call it mubasharah, and if indirectly, they call it tawlid. At this point, the author has written a hashia in which he presents the Ash'ari refutation against the Mu'tazila. 'And the Ash'ari's qiyas in their refutation of initial nazar to recollection, since there is no difference between them regarding the entailment of the required from the validity of matter and form, is refuted by the difference that recollection occurs after the acquisition of knowledge while initial [nazar] is before it, as in the introduction of Sharh al-Mawaqif. And this refutation is itself refuted by what is in al-Nihaya: that their doctrine is that when one is heedless of nazar and knowledge of the object of nazar, then recollects nazar, knowledge is not generated by it, rather it is within one's power, directly by power, so that the obligation of knowledge is not prevented. End.' Explanation of the hashia: In the mentioned hashia, the Ash'aris first refute the Mu'tazila's false idea of tawlid by stating that knowledge in itself is possible, and every possible is within divine power, so knowledge is within divine power, and nothing within power is outside power, so its occurrence without power is impossible, hence tawlid is impossible. Then the Ash'aris proceeded to invalidate the Mu'tazili doctrine and said: Recollection of nazar is, by the consensus of us and the Mu'tazila, not generative of knowledge, so initial nazar also will not generate knowledge, because both share in the nature of nazar. Therefore, the Ash'aris, in refuting the Mu'tazila, analogized initial nazar to recollection of nazar and said: If knowledge were obtained by tawlid as the Mu'tazila claim, then recollection of nazar should also be productive of knowledge, because there is no difference between initial nazar and recollection of nazar in terms of entailing the required from validity of matter and form. However, recollection of nazar, even according to the Mu'tazila, does not generate knowledge. Thus they said: 'Nazar that is repeated does not generate knowledge,' so by this analogy, initial nazar will also not generate knowledge. Refutation of the Ash'ari qiyas: This qiyas of the Ash'aris has been refuted, as in the introduction of Sharh al-Mawaqif: The analogy of recollection of nazar to initial nazar is not valid because the acquisition of knowledge from recollection is non-existent; since recollection occurs after knowledge has been obtained, then if the same knowledge were obtained again from recollection, it would entail repetition of the acquired. In contrast, initial nazar occurs before the acquisition of knowledge; so if knowledge is obtained from initial nazar, it does not entail repetition. Therefore, analogy of initial nazar to recollection of nazar is an analogy with a difference. Rebuttal: The objection raised against the Ash'aris' qiyas from the Mu'tazila side is answered by the Ash'aris in al-Nihaya. The gist of the answer is that the statement of the Ash'aris is not about absolute recollection of nazar, but about that recollection which occurs after heedlessness of acquired knowledge. And it is very clear that before this recollection there is no knowledge. Thus, even according to the Mu'tazila, this recollection is not generative of knowledge. Additionally...
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute between the Ash'ari and Mu'tazili schools on whether human speculative reasoning (nazar) generates knowledge (tawlid). The Ash'ari position, which aligns with the Hanafi school in usul al-fiqh, holds that knowledge from nazar is directly created by Allah, not produced by the act itself. The Mu'tazila, by contrast, claim that nazar generates knowledge through a process of tawlid, where one act (nazar) necessarily gives rise to another (knowledge), analogous to the movement of a key following the movement of a hand. The author first explains the Mu'tazili theory, then presents the Ash'ari refutation. The Ash'aris argue that if nazar generated knowledge, then recollection of nazar (tadhakkur) should also generate knowledge—which even the Mu'tazila deny. Since both are acts of nazar, the analogy shows the Mu'tazili position is inconsistent. However, critics (from Sharh al-Mawaqif) point out a key difference: initial nazar occurs before knowledge exists, while recollection occurs after knowledge was already present. Thus generating knowledge from recollection would be a repetition (tahsil al-hasil), which is impossible, whereas initial nazar does not have this problem. The Ash'aris respond (from al-Nihaya) that their argument is not about absolute recollection, but about a specific case: when a person is heedless of previously known knowledge and then recollects, this recollection produces knowledge anew, and even the Mu'tazila admit this type does not involve tawlid. Thus the Ash'ari position remains sound.

Key Terms
توليد (tawlid): The Mu'tazili theory that one act (e.g., nazar) necessarily gives existence to another act (e.g., knowledge) through a causal chain, similar to the key's movement being generated by the hand's movement.
نظر (nazar): Speculative reasoning or intellectual consideration aimed at acquiring knowledge, especially knowledge of Allah.
تذکر (tadhakkur): Recollection or remembering a previously known object of nazar after heedlessness.
ابتدا النظر (ibtida' al-nazar): The initial act of speculative reasoning before any knowledge has been acquired.
مباشرت (mubasharah): The direct performance of an act by an agent without any intermediate cause.
تحصيل الحاصل (tahsil al-hasil): Repetition of what has already been obtained; an impossibility in causal reasoning because one cannot acquire what is already present.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazila, what is the relationship between nazar and knowledge?
A) Allah directly creates knowledge after nazar.
B) Nazar generates knowledge through a process called tawlid.
C) Knowledge is innate and nazar merely unveils it.
D) There is no relationship; knowledge is acquired independently.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari/Hanafi position that knowledge from nazar is a direct creation of Allah, not generated by human acts, is upheld through a refined analogical argument that distinguishes between initial nazar and recollection after heedlessness.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
The Ash'arī-Mu'tazilī Debate on Tawallud of Knowledge from Nazar
Presents Ashʿarī refutation of Muʿtazilī tawallud and subsequent counter-arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Ash'arī refutation of Mu'tazilī tawallud theory and the Hanafī position that knowledge is directly from God.

Core Idea
Knowledge is not generated by reflection; all possible things are within God's power alone.

This lesson explores a foundational debate in uṣūl al-fiqh and kalām: does intellectual speculation (naẓar) generate knowledge of God? The Muʿtazila argued that initial naẓar produces knowledge by tawallud (generation), while the Ashʿarīs (and later the Ḥanafīs) insisted that knowledge is a direct act of God, with naẓar merely a condition. The disagreement has profound implications for human responsibility and the nature of divine power.

Guided Path
1
State the Ashʿarī position and its initial proof
Identify the claim that knowledge is a possible thing and thus must be within divine power; tawallud would imply human power over possible things, which is impossible. Then follow the qiyās argument: if initial naẓar generated knowledge, then tadhakkur (recollection) should also generate, but the Muʿtazila themselves deny that. Therefore, their claim is inconsistent.
The qiyās rests on the shared attribute of being a type of naẓar aimed at knowledge.
2
Examine the Muʿtazilī objection to the qiyās
The Muʿtazila reject the analogy because tadhakkur occurs after knowledge is already present; generating it again would be taḥṣīl al-ḥāṣil (acquisition of the already acquired). Initial naẓar occurs before knowledge, so no such absurdity arises. Thus, the analogy is flawed.
This objection distinguishes the two cases based on temporal order relative to knowledge.
3
Analyze the Ashʿarī rebuttal from al-Nihāyah
The Ashʿarīs specify that the relevant tadhakkur is not after knowledge but after forgetfulness (ghafla), when no knowledge remains. In that state, the recollection is exactly analogous to initial naẓar: both occur in the absence of knowledge. Therefore, the Muʿtazilī objection fails.
This refines the scope of the qiyās, showing the supposed difference is illusory.
4
Consider the Muʿtazilī alternative distinction
The Muʿtazila further claim that tadhakkur is not a voluntary human act (it occurs necessarily from God), whereas initial naẓar is voluntary and within human power. Hence, only initial naẓar can be a cause of knowledge via tawallud.
This introduces a distinction based on human capability (qudra).
5
Conclude with the Ashʿarī/Ḥanafī response and practical consequence
The Ashʿarīs counter that after forgetfulness, both initial naẓar and tadhakkur are equally non-knowledge-bearing; the voluntary/involuntary distinction does not change the fact that knowledge is absent in both cases. Therefore, the Muʿtazilī position is unsupported. The Ḥanafī school adopts the Ashʿarī view: naẓar does not generate knowledge; God directly grants knowledge after naẓar, making naẓar a condition (sharṭ), not a cause.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilāf) is whether the duty to know God is directly fulfilled by human effort or requires divine grant.

بعد حصول العلم والابتداء قبله كذا فى مقدمات شرح المواقف وهذا الدفع مدفوع بمافى النهاية من أن مذهبهم انه اذا غفل عن النظر والعلم بالمنظور فيه ثم تذكر النظر فانه لايتولد العلم به بل يكون مقدوراً بنفسه مباشرا بالقدرة لئلا يمتنع التكليف بالمعرفة انتهت
توضیح حاشیہ:۔ حاشیہ مذکورہ میں اشاعرہ نے پہلے معتزلہ کے خیال باطل تولید کو باطل کیا ہے بایں طور که علم فی نفسہ ممکن ہے اور ہرممکن مقدور الہی ہے لہذا علم مقدور الہی ہوا اور کوئی مقدور تحت قدرت سے خارج نہیں پس اسکا وقوع بغیر قدرت ممتنع لہذا تولید ممتنع ہوا۔ پھر اشاعرہ مذہب معتزلہ کے ابطال کے درپے ہوئے تو کہا تذکر نظر ہمارے معتزلہ کے اتفاق سے مولد علم نہیں اس لئے ابتداء نظر بھی مولد علم نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ دونوں نظریت میں مشترک ہیں اس لئے حضرات اشاعرہ نے معتزلہ پر رد کرتے ہوئے ابتداء نظر کا تذکر نظر پر قیاس کیا ہے اور کہا ہے کہ اگر علم تولید سے حاصل ہوتا جیسا کہ معتزلہ کا زعم ہے تو تذکر نظر کو بھی مفید علم ہونا چاہئے کیونکہ ابتداء نظر اور تذکر نظر میں مطلوب کے مستلزم ہونے کے اعتبار سے کوئی فرق نہیں ہے حالانکہ تذکر نظر معتزلہ کے نزدیک بھی مولد علم نہیں ہوتا چنانچہ انہوں نے کہا ہے کہ نظر معاد مولد علم نہیں ہوتا پس اس قیاس پر ابتداء نظر بھی مولد علم نہیں ہو گا۔ رد قیاس اشاعرہ :۔ اشاعرہ کا یہ قیاس رد کر دیا گیا ہے چنانچہ شرح مواقف کے مقدمہ میں ہے کہ تذکر نظر کا قیاس ابتداء نظر پر صحیح نہیں کیونکہ تذکر سے علم کا حصول کالعدم ہے چونکہ تذکر نظر علم حاصل ہونے کے بعد ہوتا ہے پھر اگر تذکر نظر سے پھر وہی علم حاصل ہو تو تحصیل حاصل لازم آئے گا اس کے برعکس ابتداء نظر علم کے حصول سے پہلے ہوتا ہے پس اگر ابتدائے نظر سے علم حاصل ہو تو تحصیل حاصل لازم نہیں آتا ہے لہذا ابتداء نظر کا قیاس تذکر نظر پر قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔
دفع : اشاعرہ کے ذکر کردہ قیاس پر بجانب معتزلہ جو اعتراض کیا گیا اس اعتراض کا جواب اشاعرہ کی طرف سے نہایہ میں دیا گیا ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اشاعرہ کا کلام، مطلق تذکر نظر کے بارے میں نہیں ہے بلکہ اس تذکر میں ہے جو حصول علم سے غفلت طاری ہو جانے کے بعد حاصل ہوتا ہے اور یہ بہت ظاہر ہے کہ اس تذکر سے پیشتر علم نہیں ہوتا چنانچہ معتزلہ کے نزدیک بھی یہ تذکر مولد علم نہیں، علاوہ
ازیں تذکر نظر اور ابتداء نظر کے درمیان حصول علم کے اعتبار سے کوئی فرق نہیں لہذا معتزلہ نے تذکر نظر اور ابتدائے نظر کے درمیان جو فرق واضح کیا ہے کہ تذکر نظر غیر مقدور البشر ہے اس کا وقوع بطریق ضرورت ہوتا ہے اس میں بندہ کو مطلقا اختیار نہیں رہتا کہ وہ اللہ عز شانہ کے افعال میں سے ہے افعال مکلفین سے نہیں اس لئے بندہ کو تذکر نظر کا مکلف بنانا درست نہیں ورنہ فعل غیر سے مکلف بنانا ہوگا جو درست نہیں، اس کے برخلاف ابتدائے نظر بندہ کا فعل ہے مقد در البشر ہے چنانچہ بندہ اپنی قدرت نظریہ سے علم و معرفت کو وجود دیتا ہے تا کہ تکلیف معرفت ممتنع نہ ہو جائے تو اس طرح معتزلہ کا فرق دکھانا صحیح نہیں کیونکہ حصول علم سے غفلت کے بعد تذکر نظر اور ابتداء نظر دونوں علم مطلوب کے عدم حصول میں برابر ہیں اس لئے اس کی کوئی وجہ نہیں ہے کہ ابتدائے نظر کے لئے افادہ علم کا قول کیا جائے اور تذکر کے لئے عدم افادہ کا قول کیا جائے۔
After the attainment of knowledge and the beginning before it, likewise in the Muqaddamat Sharh al-Mawaqif. And this refutation is itself refuted by what is in al-Nihayah: that their doctrine is that when one is heedless of reflection and knowledge of the object of reflection, then recollects the reflection, knowledge is not generated by it, but rather it is within His power directly by His power, so that the obligation of knowledge is not impossible. End. Clarification of the commentary: In the aforementioned commentary, the Ash'aris first refuted the Mu'tazila's false idea of tawallud, in this manner: knowledge in itself is possible, and every possible is within divine power, thus knowledge is within divine power, and nothing within power is outside power, so its occurrence without power is impossible, thus tawallud is impossible. Then the Ash'aris proceeded to refute the Mu'tazila's doctrine, saying: Recollection (tadhakkur) of reflection, by the agreement of us and the Mu'tazila, does not generate knowledge, therefore initial reflection also does not generate knowledge, because both are common in being reflections. Therefore the Ash'aris, in refuting the Mu'tazila, analogized initial reflection to recollection of reflection and said: If knowledge were acquired through generation, as the Mu'tazila claim, then recollection of reflection should also yield knowledge, because there is no difference between initial reflection and recollection of reflection in terms of leading to the desired object, even though recollection of reflection does not generate knowledge according to the Mu'tazila themselves. Thus they said: Repetitive reflection (nazar mu'ad) does not generate knowledge, so by this analogy initial reflection also will not generate knowledge. Refutation of the Ash'ari analogy: This Ash'ari analogy has been refuted. As stated in the Muqaddimat Sharh al-Mawaqif: The analogy of recollection of reflection to initial reflection is not correct, because the acquisition of knowledge from recollection is like non-existence, since recollection of reflection occurs after knowledge has been obtained; then if that same knowledge were obtained again from recollection, it would entail tahsil al-hasil (acquisition of the already acquired). In contrast, initial reflection occurs before the acquisition of knowledge; so if knowledge is obtained from initial reflection, tahsil al-hasil is not entailed. Therefore, analogizing initial reflection to recollection of reflection is an analogy with a difference. Daf' (Refutation): The objection raised by the Mu'tazila against the Ash'ari analogy is answered by the Ash'aris in al-Nihayah. The gist of the answer is: The Ash'ari's statement is not about absolute recollection of reflection, but about that recollection which occurs after heedlessness of the acquisition of knowledge has set in. It is very clear that before this recollection there is no knowledge. So according to the Mu'tazila as well, this recollection does not generate knowledge. Moreover, between this recollection and initial reflection there is no difference in terms of acquisition of knowledge. Therefore, the distinction the Mu'tazila made between recollection and initial reflection — that recollection is not within human power, its occurrence is by way of necessity, the servant has absolutely no choice in it, it is among the acts of God, not among the acts of the obligated, so it is not correct to obligate the servant with recollection, otherwise it would be obligating with another's act, which is not correct; in contrast, initial reflection is the servant's act, within human power, so the servant by his reflective power brings knowledge and cognition into existence so that the obligation of knowledge is not impossible — this distinction is not correct, because after heedlessness of the acquisition of knowledge, both recollection and initial reflection are equal in the non-acquisition of the desired knowledge. Therefore there is no reason to say that initial reflection yields knowledge and recollection does not.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of a theological and usuli dispute between the Ash'aris and the Mu'tazila over whether reflection (nazar) generates (tuwallid) knowledge of God. The author first summarizes the Ash'ari refutation of the Mu'tazilī theory of tawallud, which holds that knowledge is a possible thing and hence must be within divine power; therefore tawallud (generation of knowledge by human action) is impossible. The Ash'aris then use a qiyās (analogy) argument: if initial reflection (ibtidā' nazar) generated knowledge, then recollection of reflection (tadhakkur nazar) should also generate it, since both are acts of reflection aiming at knowledge. But the Mu'tazila themselves admit that recollection does not generate knowledge; therefore their claim that initial reflection does generate is inconsistent. The Mu'tazila respond by rejecting the analogy, arguing that recollection occurs after knowledge is already present, so generating it would be tahsīl al-hāṣil (acquisition of the already acquired), whereas initial reflection occurs before knowledge, so no such problem arises. The Ash'aris rebut this in their work al-Nihāyah by specifying that the recollection in question is not after knowledge but after forgetfulness — where no knowledge remains — making it analogous to initial reflection. The Mu'tazila then try to differentiate by saying recollection is not within human power (it occurs necessarily from God), while initial reflection is a human voluntary act. The Ash'aris counter that in the state of forgetfulness, both reflection and recollection are equally not-yet-knowledge-producing, so the distinction fails. The Hanafī school, like the Ash'aris, rejects tawallud and holds that knowledge of God is attained by God's direct grant after sincere reflection; reflection does not cause knowledge but is a condition for it.

Key Terms
تولّد (tawallud): The theory that one thing generates another; specifically, that reflection (nazar) produces knowledge as its direct effect, as held by the Mu'tazila.
نظر (nazar): Reflection or intellectual speculation aimed at acquiring knowledge, especially knowledge of God.
تذکر نظر (tadhakkur nazar): Recollection of a previous reflection; a mental act of remembering or repeating the process of reflection.
تحصیل حاصل (tahsil hasil): Acquisition of the already acquired; a logical fallacy where one tries to obtain what is already possessed.
قدرت (qudra): Power; specifically, the divine power that controls all possible things.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do the Ash'aris argue that initial reflection (ibtidā' nazar) cannot generate knowledge, according to the qiyas with tadhakkur?
A) Because tadhakkur generates knowledge, so initial reflection would be redundant.
B) Because tadhakkur does not generate knowledge, so initial reflection should also not generate, as both are reflections.
C) Because initial reflection is not within human power.
D) Because the Mu'tazila agree that tadhakkur generates knowledge.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects tawallud: knowledge of God is a divine gift, not a generated product of human reflection.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Four Schools on Nazar and Knowledge: A Hanafi Critique
Compares and critiques four views on nazar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the positions of the Mu'tazila, Hukama, Ash'ari, and Imam al-Razi on how nazar leads to knowledge, and state the Hanafi view that nazar is a preparatory cause (illa mu'idda).

Core Idea
Nazar prepares the mind; knowledge is a divine gift, not a human product.

This passage from Ashraf al-Nu'ut Sharh Muslim al-Thubut presents a key usul dispute: how does speculative reasoning (nazar) lead to knowledge? The commentator examines four schools, rejects two (Mu'tazila and Ash'ari), and endorses the view of Imam al-Razi, which aligns with the Hanafi position. Understanding this debate clarifies the Hanafi epistemological framework for ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four positions
Read the passage to extract the core claim of each school: Mu'tazila, Hukama (philosophers), Ash'ari, and Imam al-Razi. Note their view on the role of nazar and the source of knowledge.
The Mu'tazila distinguish between tadhakkur and ibtida', the Hukama propose preparation (i'dad), Ash'ari denies any causal role, and al-Razi posits 'adah ilahiyya.
2
Analyze the critique of the Mu'tazila
The author argues that the Mu'tazila distinction between tadhakkur (unwilled) and ibtida' (willed) is invalid because both are equal in not producing knowledge when one is unaware. Understand why this refutation is based on rational equality.
Key point: if both fail to produce knowledge in the same situation, they cannot be differentiated in terms of causal power.
3
Understand the philosophers' model
The Hukama hold that nazar prepares the mind (i'dad), after which knowledge flows necessarily from the Bestowing Origin (mabda' fayyad). Note that necessity here is rational, not causal for nazar.
This model preserves divine agency while giving nazar a preparatory role.
4
Analyze the rebuttal of Imam al-Ash'ari
The author declares Ash'ari's view false because rational intuition (badaha aqliyya) shows that nazar must have at least a subordinate role; otherwise knowledge would occur without it.
This is the foundational dalil aqli in the passage.
5
Locate the Hanafi alignment
The author prefers Imam al-Razi's view that after nazar, knowledge becomes necessary by divine habit ('adah), not by nazar's own power. This balances human effort with divine omnipotence and aligns with the Hanafi theory of kasb.
The example of rizq (sustenance) illustrates: Allah provides, but effort (nazar) is required.
